The lack of energy in the line mentioned at 36:02 could be contributed to the fact that Mario is unfamiliar with this new world he's found himself in. He sounds unsure of himself and everything around him. So while he sounds eager for the adventure, he's not confident in himself to give the kind of energy we usual hear in the games. Not all people are immediately full of confidence when approaching unknowns, after all. He sounds like he has a enthusiastic amount of 'Lets do this, but let's do this carefully.' It is a high possibility that as his adventure continues, his confidence will grow and his energy will grow alongside it, delivering that 'Lets'a GO!' line and attitude we've grown to known and love.

Chris Pratt is having the same issue that Dream had with his face reveal and that's pride. Dream had a lot of his streaming friends do like "I saw dreams face" videos where they are bubbly and excited and in awe and all that, so when Dream revealed his face and he was just some guy (tm), everyone gave him tons of backlash and called him ugly despite him being conventionally attractive--just a bit plain.   Chris Pratt wanted to reassure audiences that he could do a good job, but instead of taking the humble approach of "I understand that this is a big deal for Mario fans, so I'm going to do my best to make the fandom proud" he leaned into the "I nailed it guys. you are not ready for this!"   cause that's the thing. bad accents are pretty common in media. not nailing the accent, but still getting the emotion and feel of things is usually pretty forgiven when the audience isn't made to feel like it's going to be perfect. But Chris made the level of expectation too high. And it does suck cause Mario and Luigi are going to be the only characters that have accents rooted in our real society so it's more pressure for Chris. if someone else sounds stupid, we all have the ability to say "oh that's just country mushroom kingdom accent" and move on. But that's why it would have been SO SO important to take the humble approach in advertising.   Going back to Jack Black's stuff relating to the movie, it's just all about his excitement and then leaning on the comedic ("I had to learn how to breathe fire" and talking of packing on Koopa muscle for a CGI role), so we had 0 expectation for his voice aside from capturing emotions as the baseline for any voice actor. I think even if Jack was playing Mario, a failed new york accent would have been forgiven because he nailed his excitement and likely wouldn't have even addressed accents in interviews. just been like "I'm having so much fun with this, you guys, and I hope it's just as fun watching as it was being a part of it."   anyway, there is my little soap box on that.

No Chris Pratt pausing before he said koopas was not really that funny, especially considering they weren't even called kupas in the original 1983 Mario arcade game
The arcade game "Mario Bros" (1983) did not have koopas. It had turtles, crabs, flies, etc... It wasn't until '85-'86 that Super Mario Bros would introduce koopas. I think most people associate SMB with playing at home on the NES. In fact, Super Mario Bros only released on the Famicom/NES and Nintendo VS platforms unlike Mario Brothers which was released on almost anything you can imagine, including carts for various Atari machines and on diskette for computer systems. I played hours and hours of Mario Bros on my Commodore 64. It's weird to hear Pratt talk about Koopas in the arcade. I personally never saw a Super Mario arcade cabinet, but apparently they existed.

Ok I'm fully expecting a bunch of hate for this but hear me out here.   If I remember, Charles Martinet said that he couldn't do the voice of Mario for the movie because he isn't like the regular voice actors doing this as part of their job for animated shows and movies for HOURS on end.  I went looking, and Charles Martinet's first casting of Mario was for the Super Mario Bros. PINBALL GAME in 1992, where he went uncredited and unpaid for it!  Back when voice acting wasn't considered that important in video games yet........*flashbacks to Mega Man 8 voice acting and the Mega Man X4 Zero scream.......shutters*  It was after that that he did Mario teaches Typing and Mario's Game Gallery for the computers until FINALLY, in 1996, he was cast for Mario OFFICIALLY in Super Mario 64!    I know people are bitter that Martinet isn't Mario in this. Still, if you think about it, Charles Martinet is not a seasoned voice actor like Steve Blum, Johnny Yong Bosch, and MANY other talented voice actors who have fantastic RANGE to their voices.    Voice acting wasn't a huge deal until the turn of the century, and they were still trying to perfect 3d modeling in gaming lol.     Martinet will ALWAYS be Mario (THAT IS NO QUESTION!!), but I don't think it's fair to bash Chris Pratt for 2 lines of dialog in a 2 to 3-minute-long trailer. Honestly, this was more of a teaser!  That part in the trailer was merely a BLIP of what is going on in the movie.   When I get to finally see the movie, I'll tell ya then what I think.  I wonder if Nintendo and Illumination took a look at Chris's performance Onward as Barley and as Emmett in the Lego Movies and were impressed with him.  Who knows guys.  There are many reasons for the decisions behind the scenes.   I just see a lot of complaining for something that isn't really in their control. Don't get me started on people's whining and complaining about their characters not getting into Smash Bros Ultimate.......yesh.....
Honestly, I have every intention of boycotting this movie. In general I'm pissed at this trend of casting "celebrities" over actual, talented voice actors. The fact that they have an amazing voice actor for Mario for decades and decided to just push him aside for low energy Chris Pratt is so infuriating. Stop undervaluing voice actors!!!!

This might be because making movies has always been about real acting and they look down on animation because it's "childish." I don't agree with it or understand it. It's somewhat like people using AI to add frames to animation to make it smoother and it's therefore better. Mario may spend the movie finding himself. So why, when he's still so unsure about everything, would he be energetic about exploring a world he's so unfamiliar with? May be a script choice to make Mario feel that bit awkward to highlight he doesn't originate in Mushroom Kingdom, and as the movie goes on we'll gain more of that "ya-hoo!" Enthusiasm  People forget that voice acting is challenging. You are in a sound proofed room with a mic and lines, meanwhile through a grass window you've got the audio crew and directors giving tips. It is far different than any other acting where you have to actively imagine and ignore that fact that you're in a box, not actually stomping... koopas. Voice actors sometimes don't get the recognition that deserve in the acting space because their not physically being in character on a set. But it's a whole challenge in itself to act without any costume, make up, or set. Some are lucky and get to share booths with another actor like Adventure Time is known for, but you still need to engage in your imagination hard and see that other person as an actively threatening fire breathing dragon turtle.

Unpopular opinion: Pratt is a fine voice choice for Mario.  Here is why, guaranteed this will not be the only Mario movie. The OG Mario voice we all know and love is from Charles Martinet who is 67 years old. Realistically speaking, large Illumination franchise movies go on for YEARS (Despicable Me, Sing, Secret Life of Pets etc.) so Illumination needed a youthful voice that will stand the test of time.  Plus Pratt has done a number of animated movies so realistically he was the no-brainer choice.  Also, youthful audiences (which is what this movie is targeting) will love the familiar Pratt voice.  This movie will be a power house for profit and a massive resurgence in a character that young audiences don‚Äôt have much experience in.  Older audiences may hate this movie but if you focus on your love for Nintendo, this could be a beautiful revamp for a generationally known and loved franchise.
